Accounting year 10-11 Cambridge lessons
Lesson Number|Subject|Year/Grade|Topic|Learning Objective
1|Accounting|Years 10-11|1.1 The purpose of accounting|understand and explain the difference between book-keeping and accounting
2|Accounting|Years 10-11|1.1 The purpose of accounting|state the purposes of measuring business profit and loss
3|Accounting|Years 10-11|1.1 The purpose of accounting|explain the role of accounting in providing information for monitoring progress and decision-making
4|Accounting|Years 10-11|1.2 The accounting equation|explain the meaning of assets; liabilities and ownerâ€™s equity
5|Accounting|Years 10-11|1.2 The accounting equation|explain and apply the accounting equation
6|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|outline the double entry system of book-keeping
7|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|process accounting data using the double entry system
8|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|prepare ledger accounts
9|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|post transactions to the ledger accounts
10|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|balance ledger accounts as required and make transfers to financial statements
11|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|interpret ledger accounts and their balances
12|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.1 The double entry system of book-keeping|recognise the division of the ledger into the sales ledger; the purchases ledger and the nominal (general) ledger
13|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.2 Business documents|recognise and understand the following business documents: invoice; debit note; credit note; statement of account; cheque; receipt
14|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.2 Business documents|complete pro-forma business documents
15|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.2 Business documents|understand the use of business documents as sources of information: invoice; credit note; cheque counterfoil; paying-in slip; receipt; bank statement
16|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|explain the advantage of using various books of prime entry
17|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|explain the use of and process accounting data in the books of prime entry: cash book; petty cash book; sales journal; purchases journal; sales returns journal; purchases returns journal and the general journal
18|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|post the ledger entries from the books of prime entry
19|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|distinguish between and account for trade discount and cash discounts
20|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|explain the dual function of the cash book as a book of prime entry and as a ledger account for bank and cash
21|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|explain the use of and record payments and receipts made by bank transfers and other electronic means
22|Accounting|Years 10-11|2.3 Books of prime entry|explain and apply the imprest system of petty cash

Biology year 10-11 Cambridge lessons
Lesson Number|Subject|Year/Grade|Topic|Learning Objective
1|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe movement as an action by an organism or part of an organism causing a change of position or place
2|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe respiration as the chemical reactions in cells that break down nutrient molecules and release energy for metabolism
3|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe sensitivity as the ability to detect and respond to changes in the internal or external environment
4|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe growth as a permanent increase in size and dry mass
5|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe reproduction as the processes that make more of the same kind of organism
6|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe excretion as the removal of the waste products of metabolism and substances in excess of requirements
7|Biology|Years 10-11|1.1 Characteristics of living organisms|describe nutrition as the taking in of materials for energy; growth and development
8|Biology|Years 10-11|1.2 Concept and uses of classification systems|state that organisms can be classified into groups by the features that they share
9|Biology|Years 10-11|1.2 Concept and uses of classification systems|describe a species as a group of organisms that can reproduce to produce fertile offspring
10|Biology|Years 10-11|1.2 Concept and uses of classification systems|describe the binomial system of naming species as an internationally agreed system in which the scientific name of an organism is made up of two parts showing the genus and species
11|Biology|Years 10-11|1.2 Concept and uses of classification systems|construct and use dichotomous keys based on identifiable features

14|Biology|Years 10-11|1.2 Concept and uses of classification systems|explain that groups of organisms which share a more recent ancestor (are more closely related) have base sequences in DNA that are more similar than those that share only a distant ancestor

87|Science|Stage 3|3Pf3|Explore how forces can change the shape of objects
88|Science|Stage 3|3Pf4|Explore how forces; including friction; can make objects move faster or slower or change direction
89|Science|Stage 4|4Ep1|Collect evidence in a variety of contexts
90|Science|Stage 4|4Ep2|Test an idea or prediction based on scientific knowledge and understanding
91|Science|Stage 4|4Ep3|Suggest questions that can be tested and make predictions; communicate these
92|Science|Stage 4|4Ep4|Design a fair test and plan how to collect sufficient evidence
93|Science|Stage 4|4Ep5|Choose apparatus and decide what to measure
94|Science|Stage 4|4Eo1|Make relevant observations and comparisons in a variety of contexts
95|Science|Stage 4|4Eo2|Measure temperature; time; force and length

97|Science|Stage 4|4Eo4|Present results in drawings; bar charts and tables
98|Science|Stage 4|4Eo5|Identify simple trends and patterns in results and suggest explanations for some of these
99|Science|Stage 4|4Eo6|Explain what the evidence shows and whether it supports predictions. Communicate this clearly to others
100|Science|Stage 4|4Eo7|Link evidence to scientific knowledge and understanding in some contexts
101|Science|Stage 4|4Bh1|Know that humans (and some animals) have bony skeletons inside their bodies
102|Science|Stage 4|4Bh2|Know how skeletons grow as humans grow; support and protect the body
103|Science|Stage 4|4Bh3|Know that animals with skeletons have muscles attached to the bones
104|Science|Stage 4|4Bh4|Know how a muscle has to contract (shorten) to make a bone move and muscles act in pairs
105|Science|Stage 4|4Bh5|Explain the role of drugs as medicines
106|Science|Stage 4|4Be1|Investigate how different animals are found in different habitats and are suited to the environment in which they are found
107|Science|Stage 4|4Be2|Use simple identification keys
108|Science|Stage 4|4Be3|Recognise ways that human activity affects the environment; e.g. river pollution; recycling waste
109|Science|Stage 4|4Cs1|Know that matter can be solid; liquid or gas
110|Science|Stage 4|4Cs2|Investigate how materials change when they are heated and cooled
111|Science|Stage 4|4Cs3|Know that melting is when a solid turns into a liquid and is the reverse of freezing
112|Science|Stage 4|4Cs4|Observe how water turns into steam when it is heated but on cooling the steam turns back into water
113|Science|Stage 4|4Ps1|Explore how sounds are made when objects; materials or air vibrate and learn to measure the volume of sound in decibels with a sound level meter
114|Science|Stage 4|4Ps2|Investigate how sound travels through different materials to the ear
115|Science|Stage 4|4Ps3|Investigate how some materials are effective in preventing sound from travelling through them
116|Science|Stage 4|4Ps4|Investigate the way pitch describes how high or low a sound is and that high and low sounds can be loud or soft. Secondary sources can be used
117|Science|Stage 4|4Ps5|Explore how pitch can be changed in musical instruments in a range of ways
118|Science|Stage 4|4Pm1|Construct complete circuits using switch; cell (battery); wire and lamps
119|Science|Stage 4|4Pm2|Explore how an electrical device will not work if there is a break in the circuit
120|Science|Stage 4|4Pm3|Know that electrical current flows and that models can describe this flow; e.g. particles travelling around a circuit
121|Science|Stage 4|4Pm4|Explore the forces between magnets and know that magnets can attract or repel each other
122|Science|Stage 4|4Pm5|Know that magnets attract some metals but not others
123|Science|Stage 5|5Ep1|Know that scientists have combined evidence with creative thinking to suggest new ideas and explanations for phenomena
124|Science|Stage 5|5Ep2|Use observation and measurement to test predictions and make links
125|Science|Stage 5|5Ep3|Make predictions of what will happen based on scientific knowledge and understanding; and suggest and communicate how to test these
126|Science|Stage 5|5Ep4|Use knowledge and understanding to plan how to carry out a fair test
127|Science|Stage 5|5Ep5|Collect sufficient evidence to test an idea
128|Science|Stage 5|5Ep6|Identify factors that need to be taken into account in different contexts
129|Science|Stage 5|5Eo1|Make relevant observations

131|Science|Stage 5|5Eo3|Discuss the need for repeated observations and measurements

133|Science|Stage 5|5Eo5|Decide whether results support predictions

135|Science|Stage 5|5Eo7|Recognise and make predictions from patterns in data and suggest explanations using scientific knowledge and understanding
136|Science|Stage 5|5Eo8|Interpret data and think about whether it is sufficient to draw conclusions
137|Science|Stage 5|5Bp1|Know that plants need energy from light for growth
138|Science|Stage 5|5Bp2|Know that plants reproduce
139|Science|Stage 5|5Bp3|Observe how seeds can be dispersed in a variety of ways
140|Science|Stage 5|5Bp4|Investigate how seeds need water and warmth for germination; but not light
141|Science|Stage 5|5Bp5|Know that insects pollinate some flowers
142|Science|Stage 5|5Bp6|Observe that plants produce flowers which have male and female organs; seeds are formed when pollen from the male organ fertilises the ovum (female)
143|Science|Stage 5|5Bp7|Recognise that flowering plants have a life cycle including pollination; fertilisation; seed production; seed dispersal and germination
144|Science|Stage 5|5Cs1|Know that evaporation occurs when a liquid turns into a gas
145|Science|Stage 5|5Cs2|Know that condensation occurs when a gas turns into a liquid and that it is the reverse of evaporation
146|Science|Stage 5|5Cs3|Know that air contains water vapour and when this meets a cold surface it may condense
147|Science|Stage 5|5Cs4|Know that the boiling point of water is 100 Â°C and the melting point of ice is 0 Â°C
148|Science|Stage 5|5Cs5|Know that when a liquid evaporates from a solution the solid is left behind
149|Science|Stage 5|5Pl1|Observe that shadows are formed when light travelling from a source is blocked
150|Science|Stage 5|5Pl2|Investigate how the size of a shadow is affected by the position of the object

152|Science|Stage 5|5Pl4|Know that light intensity can be measured

154|Science|Stage 5|5Pl6|Know that we see light sources because light from the source enters our eyes

156|Science|Stage 5|5Pl8|Explore why a beam of light changes direction when it is reflected from a surface
157|Science|Stage 5|5Pb1|Explore; through modeling; that the sun does not move; its apparent movement is caused by the Earth spinning on its axis

161|Science|Stage 6|6Ep1|Consider how scientists have combined evidence from observation and measurement with creative thinking to suggest new ideas and explanations for phenomena

163|Science|Stage 6|6Ep3|Discuss how to turn ideas into a form that can be tested

167|Science|Stage 6|6Ep7|Choose which equipment to use
168|Science|Stage 6|6Eo1|Make a variety of relevant observations and measurements using simple apparatus correctly

172|Science|Stage 6|6Eo5|Evaluate repeated results

176|Science|Stage 6|6Eo9|Say if and how evidence supports any prediction made

183|Science|Stage 6|6Be3|Know how food chains can be used to represent feeding relationships in a habitat and present these in text and diagrams

science stages 7-9 Cambridge lessons
Lesson Number|Subject|Year/Grade|Topic|Learning Objective
1|Science|Stage 7|7TWSm.01|Describe the strengths and limitations of a model.
2|Science|Stage 7|7TWSm.02|Use symbols and formulae to represent scientific ideas.
3|Science|Stage 7|7TWSp.01|Identify whether a given hypothesis is testable.
4|Science|Stage 7|7TWSp.02|Describe how scientific hypotheses can be supported or contradicted by evidence from an enquiry.
5|Science|Stage 7|7TWSp.03|Make predictions of likely outcomes for a scientific enquiry based on scientific knowledge and understanding.
6|Science|Stage 7|7TWSp.04|Plan a range of investigations of different types; while considering variables appropriately; and recognise that not all investigations can be fair tests.
7|Science|Stage 7|7TWSp.05|Know the meaning of hazard symbols; and consider them when planning practical work.
8|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.01|Sort; group and classify phenomena; objects; materials and organisms through testing; observation; using secondary information; and making and using keys.
9|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.02|Decide what equipment is required to carry out an investigation or experiment and use it appropriately.
10|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.03|Evaluate whether measurements and observations have been repeated sufficiently to be reliable.
11|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.04|Take appropriately accurate and precise measurements; explaining why accuracy and precision are important.
12|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.05|Carry out practical work safely.
13|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.06|Evaluate a range of secondary information sources for their relevance and know that some sources may be biased.
14|Science|Stage 7|7TWSc.07|Collect and record sufficient observations and/or measurements in an appropriate form.
15|Science|Stage 7|7TWSa.01|Describe the accuracy of predictions; based on results; and suggest why they were or were not accurate.
16|Science|Stage 7|7TWSa.02|Describe trends and patterns in results; including identifying any anomalous results.
17|Science|Stage 7|7TWSa.03|Make conclusions by interpreting results and explain the limitations of the conclusions.
18|Science|Stage 7|7TWSa.04|Evaluate experiments and investigations; and suggest improvements; explaining any proposed changes.
19|Science|Stage 7|7TSWa.05|Present and interpret observations and measurements appropriately.
20|Science|Stage 7|7Bs.01|Understand that all organisms are made of cells and microorganisms are typically single celled.
21|Science|Stage 7|7Bs.02|Identify and describe the functions of cell structures (limited to cell membrane; cytoplasm; nucleus; cell wall; chloroplast; mitochondria and sap vacuole).
22|Science|Stage 7|7Bs.03|Explain how the structures of some specialised cells are related to their functions (including red blood cells; neurones; ciliated cells; root hair cells and palisade cells).
23|Science|Stage 7|7Bs.04|Describe the similarities and differences between the structures of plant and animal cells.
24|Science|Stage 7|7Bs.05|Understand that cells can be grouped together to form tissues; organs and organ systems.
25|Science|Stage 7|7Bp.01|Describe the seven characteristics of living organisms.
26|Science|Stage 7|7Bp.02|Discuss reasons for classifying viruses as living or non-living.
27|Science|Stage 7|7Bp.03|Describe a species as a group of organisms that can reproduce to produce fertile offspring.
28|Science|Stage 7|7Bp.04|Use and construct dichotomous keys to classify species and groups of related organisms.
29|Science|Stage 7|7Be.01|Know and describe the ecological role some microorganisms have as decomposers.
30|Science|Stage 7|7Be.02|Construct and interpret food chains and webs which include microorganisms as decomposers.
31|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.01|Understand that all matter is made of atoms; with each different type of atom being a different element.
32|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.02|Know that the Periodic Table presents the known elements in an order.
33|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.03|Know metals and non-metals as the two main groupings of elements.
34|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.04|Describe the differences between elements; compounds and mixtures; including alloys as an example of a mixture.
35|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.05|Describe a vacuum as a space devoid of matter.
36|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.06|Describe the three states of matter as solid; liquid and gas in terms of the arrangement; separation and motion of particles.
37|Science|Stage 7|7Cm.07|Use the particle model to represent elements; compounds and mixtures.
38|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.01|Understand that all substances have chemical properties and physical properties.
39|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.02|Understand that the acidity or alkalinity of a substance is a chemical property and is measured by pH.
40|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.03|Use indicators (including Universal Indicator and litmus) to distinguish between acidic; alkaline and neutral solutions.
41|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.04|Use tests to identify hydrogen; carbon dioxide and oxygen gases.
42|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.05|Describe common differences between metals and non-metals; referring to their physical properties.
43|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.06|Understand that alloys are mixtures that have different chemical and physical properties from the constituent substances.
44|Science|Stage 7|7Cp.07|Use the particle model to explain the difference in hardness between pure metals and their alloys.
45|Science|Stage 7|7Cc.01|Identify whether a chemical reaction has taken place through observations of the loss of reactants and/or the formation of products which have different properties to the reactants (including evolving a gas; formation of a precipitate or change of colour).
46|Science|Stage 7|7Cc.02|Explain why a precipitate forms; in terms of a chemical reaction between soluble reactants forming at least one insoluble product.
47|Science|Stage 7|7Cc.03|Use the particle model to describe chemical reactions.
48|Science|Stage 7|7Cc.04|Describe neutralisation reactions in terms of change of pH.
49|Science|Stage 7|7Pf.01|Describe changes in energy that are a result of an event or process.
50|Science|Stage 7|7Pf.02|Know that energy tends to dissipate and in doing so it becomes less useful.
51|Science|Stage 7|7Pf.03|Describe gravity as a force of attraction between any two objects and describe how the size of the force is related to the masses of the objects.
52|Science|Stage 7|7Pf.04|Understand that there is no air resistance to oppose movement in a vacuum.
53|Science|Stage 7|7Ps.01|Describe the vibration of particles in a sound wave and explain why sound does not travel in a vacuum.
54|Science|Stage 7|7Ps.02|Explain echoes in terms of the reflection of sound waves.
55|Science|Stage 7|7Pe.01|Use a simple model to describe electricity as a flow of electrons around a circuit.
56|Science|Stage 7|7Pe.02|Describe electrical conductors as substances that allow electron flow and electrical insulators as substances that inhibit electron flow.
57|Science|Stage 7|7Pe.03|Know how to measure the current in series circuits.
58|Science|Stage 7|7Pe.04|Describe how adding components into a series circuit can affect the current (limited to addition of cells and lamps).
59|Science|Stage 7|7Pe.05|Use diagrams and conventional symbols to represent; make and compare circuits that include cells; switches; lamps; buzzers and ammeters.
60|Science|Stage 7|7ESp.01|Describe the model of plate tectonics; in which a solid outer layer (made up of the crust and uppermost mantle) moves because of flow lower in the mantle.
61|Science|Stage 7|7ESp.02|Describe how earthquakes; volcanoes and fold mountains occur near the boundaries of tectonic plates.
62|Science|Stage 7|7ESp.03|Know that clean; dry air contains 78% nitrogen; 21% oxygen and small amounts of carbon dioxide and other gases; and this composition can change because of pollution and natural emissions.
63|Science|Stage 7|7ESc.01|Describe the water cycle (limited to evaporation; condensation; precipitation; water run-off; open water and groundwater).
64|Science|Stage 7|7ESs.01|Describe how planets form from dust and gas; which are pulled together by gravity.
65|Science|Stage 7|7ESs.02|Know that gravity is the force that holds components of the Solar System in orbit around the Sun.
66|Science|Stage 7|7ESs.03|Describe tidal forces on Earth as a consequence of the gravitational attraction between the Earth; Moon and Sun.
67|Science|Stage 7|7ESs.04|Explain how solar and lunar eclipses happen.
68|Science|Stage 7|7SIC.01|Discuss how scientific knowledge is developed through collective understanding and scrutiny over time.
69|Science|Stage 7|7SIC.02|Describe how science is applied across societies and industries; and in research.
70|Science|Stage 7|7SIC.03|Evaluate issues which involve and/or require scientific understanding.
71|Science|Stage 7|7SIC.04|Describe how people develop and use scientific understanding; as individuals and through collaboration; e.g. through peer-review.
72|Science|Stage 7|7SIC.05|Discuss how the uses of science can have a global environmental impact.

93|Science|Stage 8|8Bs.01|Identify ball-and-socket and hinge joints; and explain how antagonistic muscles move the bones at a hinge joint.

95|Science|Stage 8|8Bs.03|Describe how the structure of the human respiratory system is related to its function of gas exchange (in terms of lung structure and the action of the diaphragm and intercostal muscles) and understand the difference between breathing and respiration.

99|Science|Stage 8|8Bp.03|Discuss how human growth; development and health can be affected by lifestyle; including diet and smoking.

101|Science|Stage 8|8Bp.05|Know and use the summary word equation for aerobic respiration (glucose + oxygen -> carbon dioxide + water).
102|Science|Stage 8|8Be.01|Identify different ecosystems on the Earth; recognising the variety of habitats that exist within an ecosystem.

105|Science|Stage 8|8Cm.01|Describe the Rutherford model of the structure of an atom.

107|Science|Stage 8|8Cm.03|Know that the electrostatic attraction between positive and negative charge is what holds together individual atoms.
108|Science|Stage 8|8Cm.04|Know that purity is a way to describe how much of a specific chemical is in a mixture.
109|Science|Stage 8|8Cp.01|Understand that the concentration of a solution relates to how many particles of the solute are present in a volume of the solvent.
110|Science|Stage 8|8Cp.02|Describe how paper chromatography can be used to separate and identify substances in a sample.
111|Science|Stage 8|8Cc.01|Use word equations to describe reactions.

113|Science|Stage 8|8Cc.03|Describe the reactivity of metals (limited to sodium; potassium; calcium; magnesium; zinc; iron; copper; gold and silver) with oxygen; water and dilute acids.
114|Science|Stage 8|8Cc.04|Know that reactions do not always lead to a single pure product and that sometimes a reaction will produce an impure mixture of products.
115|Science|Stage 8|8Cc.05|Describe how the solubility of different salts varies with temperature.
116|Science|Stage 8|8Cc.06|Understand that some substances are generally unreactive and can be described as inert.
117|Science|Stage 8|8Pf.01|Calculate speed (speed = distance / time).

120|Science|Stage 8|8Pf.04|Identify and calculate turning forces (moment = force x distance).
121|Science|Stage 8|8Pf.05|Explain that pressure is caused by the action of a force; exerted by a substance; on an area (pressure = force / area).
122|Science|Stage 8|8Pf.06|Use particle theory to explain pressures in gases and liquids (qualitative only).
123|Science|Stage 8|8Pf.07|Describe the diffusion of gases and liquids as the intermingling of substances by the movement of particles.
124|Science|Stage 8|8Ps.01|Describe reflection at a plane surface and use the law of reflection.

126|Science|Stage 8|8Ps.03|Know that white light is made of many colours and this can be shown through the dispersion of white light; using a prism.
127|Science|Stage 8|8Ps.04|Describe how colours of light can be added; subtracted; absorbed and reflected.
128|Science|Stage 8|8Pe.01|Describe a magnetic field; and understand that it surrounds a magnet and exerts a force on other magnetic fields.

133|Science|Stage 8|8ESc.01|Understand that there is evidence that the Earth's climate exists in a cycle between warm periods and ice ages; and the cycle takes place over long time periods.
134|Science|Stage 8|8ESc.02|Understand that the Earth's climate can change due to atmospheric change.
135|Science|Stage 8|8ESc.03|Describe the difference between climate and weather.
136|Science|Stage 8|8ESs.01|Describe a galaxy in terms of stellar dust and gas; stars and planetary systems.
137|Science|Stage 8|8ESs.02|Describe asteroids as rocks; smaller than planets; and describe their formation from rocks left over from the formation of a planetary system.
138|Science|Stage 8|8SIC.01|Discuss how scientific knowledge is developed through collective understanding and scrutiny over time.

142|Science|Stage 8|8SIC.05|Discuss how the uses of science can have a global environmental impact.
143|Science|Stage 9|9TWSm.01|Understand that models and analogies reflect current scientific evidence and understanding and can change.
144|Science|Stage 9|9TWSm.02|Describe some important models; including analogies; and discuss their strengths and limitations.
145|Science|Stage 9|9TWSm.03|Use symbols and formulae to represent scientific ideas.

148|Science|Stage 9|9TWSp.03|Make predictions of likely outcomes for a scientific enquiry based on scientific knowledge and understanding.
149|Science|Stage 9|9TWSp.04|Plan a range of investigations of different types to obtain appropriate evidence when testing hypotheses.
150|Science|Stage 9|9TWSp.05|Make risk assessments for practical work to identify and control risks.
151|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.01|Sort; group and classify phenomena; objects; materials and organisms through testing; observation; using secondary information; and making and using keys.
152|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.02|Decide what equipment is required to carry out an investigation or experiment and use it appropriately.
153|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.03|Decide when to increase the range of observations and measurements; and increase the extent of repetition; to give sufficiently reliable data.
154|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.04|Take appropriately accurate and precise measurements; explaining why accuracy and precision are important.
155|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.05|Carry out practical work safely; supported by risk assessments where appropriate.
156|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.06|Make an informed decision whether to use evidence from first-hand experience or secondary sources.
157|Science|Stage 9|9TWSc.07|Collect; record and summarise sufficient observations and measurements; in an appropriate form.
158|Science|Stage 9|9TWSa.01|Evaluate the strength of the evidence collected and how it supports; or refutes; the prediction.
159|Science|Stage 9|9TWSa.02|Describe trends and patterns in results; identifying any anomalous results and suggesting why results are anomalous.
160|Science|Stage 9|9TWSa.03|Make conclusions by interpreting results; explain the limitations of the conclusions and describe how the conclusions can be further investigated.
161|Science|Stage 9|9TWSa.04|Evaluate experiments and investigations; including those by others; and suggest improvements; explaining any proposed changes.
162|Science|Stage 9|9TWSa.05|Present and interpret results; and predict results between the data points collected.
163|Science|Stage 9|9Bs.01|Describe the pathway of water and mineral salts from the roots to the leaves in flowering plants; including absorption in root hair cells; transport through xylem and transpiration from the surface of leaves.
164|Science|Stage 9|9Bs.02|Describe the structure of the human excretory (renal) system and its function (limited to kidneys filtering blood to remove urea; which is excreted in urine).
165|Science|Stage 9|9Bs.03|Know that chromosomes contain genes; made of DNA; and that genes contribute to the determination of an organism's characteristics.
166|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.01|Describe the fusion of gametes to produce a fertilised egg with a new combination of DNA.
167|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.02|Describe the inheritance of sex in humans in terms of XX and XY chromosomes.
168|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.03|Describe variation within a species and relate this to genetic differences between individuals.
169|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.04|Describe the scientific theory of natural selection and how it relates to genetic changes over time.
170|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.05|Know that plants require minerals to maintain healthy growth and life processes (limited to magnesium to make chlorophyll and nitrates to make protein).
171|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.06|Know that photosynthesis occurs in chloroplasts and is the process by which plants make carbohydrates; using the energy from light.
172|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.07|Know and use the summary word equation for photosynthesis (carbon dioxide + water -> glucose + oxygen; in the presence of light and chlorophyll).
173|Science|Stage 9|9Bp.08|Discuss how fetal development is affected by the health of the mother; including the effect of diet; smoking and drugs.
174|Science|Stage 9|9Be.01|Describe what could happen to the population of a species; including extinction; when there is an environmental change.
175|Science|Stage 9|9Cm.01|Understand that the structure of the Periodic Table is related to the atomic structure of the elements and the Periodic Table can be used to predict an elementâ€™s structure and properties.
176|Science|Stage 9|9Cm.02|Understand that a molecule is formed when two or more atoms join together chemically; through a covalent bond.
177|Science|Stage 9|9Cm.03|Describe a covalent bond as a bond made when a pair of electrons is shared by two atoms (limited to single bonds).
178|Science|Stage 9|9Cm.04|Describe an ion as an atom which has gained at least one electron to be negatively charged or lost at least one electron to be positively charged.
179|Science|Stage 9|9Cm.05|Describe an ionic bond as an attraction between a positively charged ion and a negatively charged ion.
180|Science|Stage 9|9Cp.01|Understand that the groups within the Periodic Table have trends in physical and chemical properties; using group 1 as an example.
181|Science|Stage 9|9Cp.02|Describe how the density of a substance relates to its mass in a defined volume.
182|Science|Stage 9|9Cp.03|Calculate and compare densities of solids; liquids and gases.
183|Science|Stage 9|9Cp.04|Know that elements and compounds exist in structures (simple or giant); and this influences their physical properties.
184|Science|Stage 9|9Cc.01|Use word equations and symbol equations to describe reactions (balancing symbol equations is not required).
185|Science|Stage 9|9Cc.02|Identify examples of displacement reactions and predict products (limited to reactions involving calcium; magnesium; zinc; iron; copper; gold and silver salts).
186|Science|Stage 9|9Cc.03|Describe how to prepare some common salts by the reactions of metals with acids; and metal carbonates with acids; and purify them; using filtration; evaporation and crystallisation.
187|Science|Stage 9|9Cc.04|Describe the effects of concentration; surface area and temperature on the rate of reaction; and explain them using the particle model.
188|Science|Stage 9|9Cc.05|Understand that in chemical reactions mass and energy are conserved.
189|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.01|Use density to explain why objects float or sink in water.
190|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.02|Describe the difference between heat and temperature.
191|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.03|Know that energy is conserved; meaning it cannot be created or destroyed.
192|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.04|Know that thermal energy will always transfer from hotter regions or objects to colder ones; and this is known as heat dissipation.
193|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.05|Describe thermal transfer by the processes of conduction; convection and radiation.
194|Science|Stage 9|9Pf.06|Explain cooling by evaporation.
195|Science|Stage 9|9Ps.01|Draw and interpret waveforms; and recognise the link between loudness and amplitude; pitch and frequency.
196|Science|Stage 9|9Ps.02|Use waveforms to show how sound waves interact to reinforce or cancel each other.
197|Science|Stage 9|9Pe.01|Describe how current divides in parallel circuits.
198|Science|Stage 9|9Pe.02|Know how to measure current and voltage in series and parallel circuits; and describe the effect of adding cells and lamps.
199|Science|Stage 9|9Pe.03|Calculate resistance (resistance = voltage / current) and describe how resistance affects current.
200|Science|Stage 9|9Pe.04|Use diagrams and conventional symbols to represent; make and compare circuits that include cells; switches; resistors (fixed and variable); ammeters; voltmeters; lamps and buzzers.
201|Science|Stage 9|9ESp.01|Explain the movement of tectonic plates in terms of convection currents.
202|Science|Stage 9|9ESp.02|Explain why the jigsaw appearance of continental coasts; location of volcanoes and earthquakes; fossil record and alignment of magnetic materials in the Earth's crust are all evidence for tectonic plates.
203|Science|Stage 9|9ESc.01|Describe the carbon cycle (limited to photosynthesis; respiration; feeding; decomposition and combustion).
204|Science|Stage 9|9ESc.02|Describe the historical and predicted future impacts of climate change; including sea level change; flooding; drought and extreme weather events.
205|Science|Stage 9|9ESs.01|Describe the consequences of asteroid collision with the Earth; including climate change and mass extinctions.
206|Science|Stage 9|9ESs.02|Describe the evidence for the collision theory for the formation of the Moon.
207|Science|Stage 9|9ESs.03|Know that nebulae are clouds of dust and gas; and can act as stellar nurseries.
208|Science|Stage 9|9SIC.01|Discuss how scientific knowledge is developed through collective understanding and scrutiny over time.
209|Science|Stage 9|9SIC.02|Describe how science is applied across societies and industries; and in research.
210|Science|Stage 9|9SIC.03|Evaluate issues which involve and/or require scientific understanding.
211|Science|Stage 9|9SIC.04|Describe how people develop and use scientific understanding as individuals and through collaboration; e.g. through peer-review.
212|Science|Stage 9|9SIC.05|Discuss how the uses of science can have a global environmental impact.
